< Text>
Bay Area Rapid Transit widely known by the acronym ‚ÄúBART‚Äù is the main rail transportation system for the San Francisco Bay Area.

1900s, the idea of an underwater electric rail tube was first proposed by Francis "Borax" Smith.

Since 1911, visionaries had periodically brought up this Jules Verne concept.

In 1946, the ‚ÄúBART‚Äù story begins as a concept gradually evolving from informal gatherings of business and civic leaders on both sides of the San Francisco Bay.  People discussed ways of easing the mounting congestion that was clogging the bridges spanning the Bay.

In 1947, a joint Army-Navy review Board concluded that another connecting link between San Francisco and Oakland would be needed in the years ahead to prevent intolerable congestion on the Bay Bridge.

In the 1950s, the actual planning for a rapid transit system began.

In 1951, California's legislature created the San Francisco Bay Area Rapid Transit Commission to study the Bay Area's long-term transportation needs.

In 1957, forming of a transit district charged with the construction and operation of a high-speed rapid rail system linking the cities and suburbs, thus BART (Bay Area Rapid Transit District) was formed.

Between 1957 and 1962, engineering plans were developed for a system of electric trains that would run on grade-separated right-of-ways, reaching maximum speeds of 75-80 mph, averaging perhaps 45 mph, including station stops.  Advanced transit cars, with sophisticated suspensions, braking and propulsion systems, and luxurious interiors.

In November 1962, the BART plans were finally approved by the voters.

In 1962, the total cost of the system was projected at $996 million.  It would be the largest single public works project ever undertaken in the U.S. by the local citizenry.

On June 19, 1964, BART construction officially began with President Lyndon Johnson presiding over the ground-breaking ceremonies at the 4.4-mile test track between Concord and Walnut Creek in Contra Costa County.

In February, 1967, the 3.2-mile bore through the hard rock of the Berkeley Hills was completed after 466 work days, to become the fourth longest vehicular tunnel in the U.S.

On January 27, 1971, the final tunnel bore was "holed through" into the west end of the Montgomery Street Station and also marked the completion of tunneling work in the huge, two-level Market Street subway and climaxed six years of tunneling underground.

On September 11, 1972, BART began service and reported more than 100,000 passengers in its first five days.

‚Ä¢	In November 1977, Saturday trains started.

‚Ä¢	In July 1978, Sunday service started.

In the 1980s an extension to the San Francisco Airport was being planned.

The 1989, the Loma Prieta earthquake severed the San Francisco ‚Äì Oakland Bay Bridge for a month and destroyed the Cypress Street Viaduct.

Our visit:
BART is a ‚Äúlove, hate, relationship.‚Äù  You love the system when it‚Äôs running on time, but hate it when it breaks down or in this case, the looming strike, which would cripple the commute by forcing hundreds of thousands of additional vehicles on the road!

I‚Äôve ridden these trains on numerous occasions over the years, especially when it first came on line.  At first, the new trains were more of a novelty and pretty crowded with a lot of sight seers and tourists.

Over the years, the tourist aspect has diminished and the system settled into the commute mode of transporting thousands of Bay Area residents, myself included during those early years.

I no longer rely on the BART system, which for me is a good thing with the latest on going squabble and possible shutting down of the system on 17 Oct 2013 would be terrible for those depending on this form of transportation.

Overall, BART has reduced a lot of the vehicle traffic that we would typically have and has been of great service, ‚Äúwhen it has operated!‚Äù<//Text>

< review>
Arrived at this Quick Lane location about 11am. Waiting area is clean and there was some left over regular coffee for customers but no decaf. Our customer service rep was Ruben and he was familiar with our auto and the discount coupon we presented.
Ruben said our wait would be about 1 1/2 hours so we took a walk around several of the local car dealers. We came back in time but unfortunately the store had a computer breakdown so we had to wait another 45 minutes. If that had not happened we would have rated 5-stars.
The outcome was as expected, and we were out the door for $37.72 for a synthetic blend oil change, filter, tire rotation, etc. Great magazine coupon. Probably not frequently available.
Something nice.. had an email this morning stating that Fiesta Ford had purchased a CARFAX report for the Honda we had serviced yesterday! No charge and good until we sold the car. That's a $99 value to go along with our discounted oil change. Not bad! Thank you Fiesta Ford!< /review>

Fantastic service and I highly recommend this shop. What can I say? Everything!
Waiting area is clean and comfortable and the coffee's always on.
The service advisors are friendly,   professional and highly knowledgeable.
The manager doesn't hide in an office but jumps in to look over the work or assist the mechanics which provides for great quality control.
You can watch the work being done through large plate glass windows in a clean well organized shop.
The work itself is done well and efficiently.
If your repairs take a long time they happily drive you wherever you want in their shuttle.
I highly recommend this repair shop. Five stars plus!< /review>

I do like this Mr. Pickles location better than most. They always have fresh ingredients and plenty of them. Service is usually good. The only thing I would recommend is to not order through Door Dash. The app will alert you that your food is ready even if it isn't. This was a big issue for me since I was starving and went in to pick up my sandwiches only to find out they hadn't even started it because they were fulfilling all walk-in orders first. So basically I placed my order at 6:30 PM and my order was ready at 7pm. I arrived at 7:05 pm to learn that anyone who walked in between 6:30 and 7:04 pm orders were  being completed and mine wasn't started. That is my only complaint. Also, in the spring and fall, if you go by on a weekend you may be lucky enough to high five Mr. Pickles himself who is waving at everyone on Castro Valley Blvd. My kids thought that was so awesome to high five him.< /text>

< text>
Although it cost $6 to get in...
It may be worth it if you are looking for a non crowded park with scenic trails and wildlife.
There are 2 restrooms which are both very clean and well kept.
Plenty of parking either way you decide to explore.
Great place to fly kites or other aerial activities because likely you'll notice people love flying here, it's very common.
Overall, this park is for everyone and it's worth the fee. Just please leave no trash behind and respect the park. Thanks!< /text>

< text>
Want to bike on calm on a nice evening, this is the best place if you are in santaclara County. Usually not very windy. Park closes at sunset. Entry during summer requires $10 per car.
Park provides very good bbq pits with lot of tree cover, tables and water. Restrooms are clean. Has very good play area for kids.

You can enjoy your kite or drowns in the vast green field.
This place is habitat for ducks, goose and you will notice jack rabbits jumping in the bushes<//text>

April 2020. Killed 7 ticks in 7 minutes.
Regular review:
Great park with ample parking. It's often quite windy, bring a jacket. There are some picnic tables but a blanket is recommended in case you came to late and need to have a barrier between you and the blood sucking ticks. Those things lay 800 eggs per cycle and can carry lymes disease!

Only issue is the smell from nearby waste facility.< /Review>

<Review>Baylands is a beautiful park at the end of Lawrence Expressway near 237.  It has very nice picnic areas and a huge grassy area.  This is the City of Sunnyvales designated remote control flying field and is very popular with drones and fixed-wing aircraft on Saturday and Sunday mornings.  A tip: this park is all but abandoned on the weekdays.  There is a $5 parking fee at the gate, but you can get a yearly pass for $20.</Review>< gmapID>

It's a pleasant place to have a walk, fly drones, have a party, or go for a run. There's even a couple of playgrounds there. But a number of cars had their windows smashed and things stolen recently. <text>This is my favorite Sunnyvale park, I buy their $25 season pass each year - without the pass it costs $6 per vehicle during the summer months (free in the winter). I'll take a camp chair and sit under the trees and read, or take pictures of the radio controlled model planes and drones (though drones have been restricted lately). There is also an impressive small animal zoo and drought tolerant garden at one end, and long trails out by the wetlands. You may see raptors and other rare birds. Reservations are required to reserve one of the many picnic areas. The rope course is not well maintained, but parts of it are usable. There are two restrooms which are open in season, one at the end of the south parking lot is usually closed.<//text><date>1549469028874< /date>< response>

<Name>Yelitza Mar√≠a<//Name><Date>1345160693066< /Date><rating>4</rating>< review>
Just got back from a trip today for a work outing. I'm rating a hesitant 2, because while it was good, I don't know that I'd call it "very good". It was a little better than just "good" though so 2 it is.

Reasons why: Overall it was a nice park, middle of the work day so not a lot of people but still enough that you don't feel like the place is abandoned. Didn't have to pay for parking and it was right next to our tables so that was also good. There's a nice little area between the trees where you could just hear birds and the breeze blowing which made for a relaxing visit. I have IBS so accessible restrooms are important to me. These were right next our tables, and surprisingly clean and well stocked. They could use a paint upgrade but overall I was pleased and comfortable with the bathrooms. The trails are nice to hike and bike and we even saw some wildlife.

The main reason why I can't give this park a 3 rating is because there was dog poop in a lot of the grassy areas and paths. Once you found an area that was free of poop then it was great but having to walk around the poop the rest of the time felt like trying to avoid mines, some areas were almost impossible.<//review>

<Name>Bryan Meyer</Name>< text>
First off, realize that you'll pay $6 per car to get into this park.  That said, they have lots of picnic areas to host a gathering and they are nicely furnished and separate.  Pros - they have the space, there's also a nice children's park/structure separate from the picnic tables areas.  However, this place gets windy by the middle of the day - I'm talking blows your hat off and blows your paper and plastic products away.  So be forewarned.  Also, apparently if you go here on a weekend morning you'll see a bunch of people flying their drones around here (no wind in the mornings).<//text>

A must for the upcoming summer months!< /text></record>
